Jamison Brereton

26 (646)
A┼Ыvins (1тАУ19), Va╠Дyu (20тАУ25)
Vi┼Ыvamanas Vaiya┼Ыva or Vya┼Ыva ─Ас╣Еgirasa
25 verses: uс╣гс╣Зih, except g─Бyatr─л 16тАУ19, 21, 25 and anuс╣гс╣нubh 20, arranged in trcas, with ╠е an extra verse, 19, at the end of the A┼Ыvin sequence
A long and rather repetitive hymn. The first nineteen verses are dedicated to the A┼Ыvins and, as usual, urge them to drive their chariot to our sacrifice and to give us goods in return. There is little novel to capture the audience; the most striking image is found in verse 13: the unnamed god Agni, dressed in sacrifices like a bride in her wedding finery.
The final six verses belong to V─Бyu, deified Wind, another god associated with the early-morning sacrifice, who receives the first soma drink there. He too is called to make the journey to our sacrifice and reward us for our offerings. He is twice (vss. 21, 22) designated as the son-in-law of Tvaс╣гс╣нar, the fashioner godтАФa somewhat surprising identification, given the tangled marital situation of Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs daughter as tantalizingly sketched in X.17.1тАУ2тАФwhere V─Бyu is not in the picture.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(A┼Ыvins) of irresistible strength, affluent showerers (of benefits), I invoke your chariot amid the pious,who are assembled to celebrate your presence.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I call your chariot for joint praise among our patrons,
o you of invincible skill, you bulls who bring bullish goods.

Griffith

I CALL your chariot to receive united praise mid princely men,
Strong Gods who pour down wealth, of never vanquished might!

Geldner

Euren Wagen rufe ich fein, um bei den reichen G├╢nnern einstimmiges Lob zu finden, ihr Bullen von un├╝bertroffener Willenskraft, ihr Schatzreichen.

Grassmann

Ich rufe euren Wagen her zum Chorlied bei der edlen Schar, O heldenstarke Helden, unbesiegt an Kraft.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(Say), Varu (thus), N─Бsaty─Бs, senders of rain, affluent showerers (of benefits), as you came toSuс╣г─Бman with your protections to (grant him) great riches, (so come to me).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Say, Varu, thus: varu, vocative: hevarun─Бmaka r─Бjan, evam br┼лh─лti с╣Ыс╣гir vadati; to grant him great riches: mahe tane = mahate dhan─Бya;mahyam ─Бy─Бtam

Jamison Brereton

O N─Бsatyas, to Varo Suс╣г─Бman for his great extension
do you drive with your help, you bulls who bring bullish goods.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAffluent in nourishment, we invoke you, who are desirous of (sacrificial) food, on this occasion at dawnwith oblations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

At dawn: ati kс╣гapaс╕е kс╣гap─Бya atikrame = at the passing of night, uс╣гaс╕е k─Бle

Jamison Brereton

We call you today with our oblations, you who bring prizewinning mares as goods,
as you become refreshed on the many refreshments beyond the nights.

Jamison Brereton Notes

hav─Бmahe havy├йbhiс╕е тАЬwe call with oblationsтАЭ is a word play between the the roots тИЪhu тАШpour, libateтАЩ and тИЪh┼л/hv─Б тАШcallтАЩ and economically refers to the two complementary aspects of Vedic sacrifice, the verbal and the material. It is the mirror image of the trope тАЬpour prayers.тАЭ iс╣г├бyantau can belong either to trans. iс╣г├бyati to тИЪiс╣г тАШsendтАЩ (so Grassmann, Lubotsky) or intrans. iс╣г├бyati тАШprosperтАЩ. I tentatively opt for the latter, with a cognate acc. of respect, iс╣г├бс╕е, hence тАЬprosper, become refreshed with respect to refreshments.тАЭ It is not entirely clear to me which root affiliation is represented by GeldnerтАЩs тАЬspendenтАЭ (probably тАШsendтАЩ?) or RenouтАЩs тАЬs├йcr├йtant ├а titre de jouissanceтАЭ (probably тАШprosperтАЩ?).

I suggest that ├бti kс╣гap├бс╕е тАЬbeyond the nightsтАЭ refers to the Atir─Бtra soma (тАЬovernight somaтАЭ) offered to the A┼Ыvins the morning after, as it were.

Griffith

So with oblations we invoke you, rich in ample wealth, to-day,
When night hath passed, O ye who send us plenteous food.
O Asvins, Heroes, let your car, famed, best to travel, come to us,
And, for his glory, mark your zealous servant’s lauds.

Geldner

Darum laden wir euch beide heute mit Opferspenden, ihr Reichlohnende, die ├╝ber die N├дchte hinweghelfend viele Labsale spenden.

Grassmann

So laden labungsreiche euch, auch heute wir durch Opfer ein; Die viele Gaben ihr auf lange Zeit verleiht.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬDasras, who are gratified by sacred rites, of fascinating complexion, lords of rain, pass with your fleet(horses) completely round our entier (sacrifice).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Complexion: madhuvarс╣З─Б = ye yuvayo r┼лpam pa┼Ыyanti tetatraiva hс╣Ыс╣гс╣н─Б bhavanti, they who look upon your beauty are delighted

Jamison Brereton

For you two wondrous ones fly around the whole (world) in proper sequence with your prompt (horses),
as those who quicken our insight, as the honey-colored lords of beauty.1084 VIII.26

Griffith

For, Wonder-Workers, with fleet steeds ye fly completely round this All,
Stirring our thoughts, ye Lords of splendour, honey-hued.

English translation:

тАЬIndra and N─Бsaty─Бs, who are most accessible, come to this my sacrifice; come, gods, today with(other) divinities.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You twoтАФcome here to receive this (offering) of mine, Indra and N─БsatyasтАФ
as two gods joined in greatest delight with the gods today.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is somewhat curiously constructed. It contains, probably, a dual dvandva whose 2nd member is itself dual: ├нndra-n─Бsaty─Б тАШo Indra and the two N─БsatyasтАЩ. Since the form is in the voc. it is actually impossible to determine if it is in fact a dual dvandva or two separate vocc., ├нndra n─Бsaty─Б, sg. and du. Although in most dual dvandvas the first member also has dual inflection (type ├нndr─Б-v├бruс╣З─Б), see indra-v─Бy┼л╠Б, with stem form in the first member and a single 2nd member accent; its voc. is ├нndra-v─Бy┼л, which would match the template found here. In any case, the verb is dual (gatam), and the rest of the verse (p─Бda c) is couched in the dual. This either means that Indra is being ignored (which is possible, since the hymn is dedicated to the A┼Ыvins) or that the dual dvandva ├нndra-n─Бsaty─Б is being treated as if it contained two entities, rather than one+two (which is also possible). For another number mismatch, see vs. 11.

Griffith

To welcome this mine offering, O ye Indra-like Nasatyas, come
As Gods of best accord this day with other Gods.

Geldner

Kommet, Indra und die Nasatya┬┤s, zu meiner Darbringung, ihr G├╢tter mit den G├╢ttern heute recht eintr├дchtig!

Grassmann

Zu diesem meinem Mahle kommt mit Indra, o ihr Treuen, her, Ihr G├╢tter mit den G├╢ttern heut in Huld vereint.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬDesirous of you who are bestowers of wealth, we invoke you, as did (your father) Vya┼Ыva; come,sagacious A┼Ыvins, here with favourable intentions.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because we call upon you, (we) seeking bulls like Vya┼Ыva seeking Ukс╣гan (his patron),
come here with your favors, o inspired poets.

Jamison Brereton Notes

vay├бm тАж ukс╣гaс╣Зy├бnto vya┼Ыvav├бt is a play on words. ukс╣гany├бntaс╕е is read doubly, in one sense in the frame (тАШseeking bullsтАЩ) and another in the simile (тАШseeking Ukс╣гanтАЩ). Unusually the simile is conveyed by -v├бt. On the poet Vya┼Ыva seeking his patron Ukс╣гan, see VIII.23.16 vy├а┼Ыvaс╕е тАж ukс╣гaс╣Зy├║с╕е, where ukс╣гany├║с╕е can also be read as a pun.

Griffith

For we, like Vyasva, lifting up our voice like oxen, call on you:
With all your loving kindness, Sages, come to us.

Denn wir rufen euch, nach einem Uksan verlangend gleich Vyasva. Kommet, ihr Redekundigen, hierher mit Wohlwollen!

Denn wie Via├зva rufen wir wie Stiere br├╝llend euch herbei, O kommt hierher, ihr weisen mit Gewogenheit.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAdorable showerers (of benefits), bestow daily upon me (some) of that (wealth) which is given by you,which is brought by you for the worshippers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O holy ones, out of what is given by you and what is brought by you, do your best for me along with my patrons day after day, o bulls.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take s┼лr├нbhiс╕е as an instr. of accompaniment тАЬfor me along with my patrons,тАЭ but GeldnerтАЩs view, that the patrons are the middlemen distributing the goods, is possible: тАЬdo your best for me by means of / through my patrons.тАЭ

Griffith

Gods whom we yearn for, of your gifts, of what ye bring to us, bestow
By princes’ hands on me, ye Mighty, day by day.

Geldner

Von dem von euch geschenkten, ihr ……., von dem von euch zugewendeten Reichtum denket mir Tag f├╝r Tag durch die freigebigen Herren etwas zu, ihr Bullen!

Grassmann

Von dem, was ihr, freigiebige, gebracht, geschenkt habt, theilet mit Mir durch die F├╝rsten Tag f├╝r Tag, o Helden ihr.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe man who is enveloped in sacrifices (offered) to you, like a woman with additional raiment,rewarding him, A┼Ыvins, you plural ce him in prosperity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Raiment: adhivastra, having another garment over herordinary clothes

Jamison Brereton

The one who is swathed in sacrifices for you, like a bride in her (wedding) dressтАФ
serving (him [=Agni]), the A┼Ыvins have made (him) to be beautifulтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the referent of ab to be Agni. Cf. III.3.5 t├бviс╣г─лbhir ─Б╠Бvr╠еtam тАШswathed with [=in] his powersтАЭ; given AgniтАЩs ritual role it makes sense for him to be swathed in sacrifices. Making a god the referent avoids the role reversal Renou notes in sapary├бnt─Б, with (in his view) the gods serving humans rather than the usual situation – though he then tr. ┼Ыubh├й cakr─Бte as reflexive or self-involved: тАЬils se sont fait (pour eux-m├кmes une parure – contrapartie de b),тАЭ rather than supplying a human object. But surely it is better (with Geldner) to supply as obj. of ┼Ыubh├й cakr─Бte the being referred to in the relative clause of ab.

Griffith

Him whom your sacrifices clothe, even as a woman with her robe,
The Asvins help to glory honouring him well.

Der ganz von eurer Verehrung angetan ist wie eine mit Kleidern bedeckte Frau, ihn ehren die Asvin und haben ihm zur Pracht verholfen;

Wer sich in eure Opfer h├╝llt, gleich wie die Braut in ihr Gewand, Den schaffen hin die Ritter, ehrend ihn, zum Gl├╝ck.

Jamison Brereton

(Agni,) who will watch over your (circuit) of broadest extent, protective of men.
Drive around your circuit, seeking us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner I take ab as a continuation of vs. 13, still with Agni as referent.

Agni is regularly called cikitv─Б╠Бn, to the same stem as c├нketati here. Clearly vart├нс╕е тАШcircuitтАЩ is to be supplied as object; it not only appears in p─Бda c but also in 15b, where it is modified by nс╣Ыp─Б╠Бyyam as here.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAffluent showerers (of benefits), come to our dwelling for (the libation) to be drunk by the leaders (ofrites), for you bring the sacrifice to completion by praise, as the fatal shaft (slays the deer).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Slays the deer:viс╣гudruheva = vi┼Ыv─Бn hinasti ┼Ыatr┼лn iti, ┼Ыaraс╕е; the allusion: tena (vi┼Ыudruha) yath─Б vy─Бdho mс╣Ыgamabhilaс╣гitam de┼Ыam pr─Бpayati tadvat stuty─Б yaj├▒am avaikalyena sam─Бptim pr─Бpayathaс╕е, as a hunter by anarrow brings the deer to the desired spot (to its destination?), so you by praise, cause the sacrifice to attaincompletion

Jamison Brereton

For us drive your circuit protective of men, you who bring
bullish goods.
As if mounting (a chariot) facing many directions, you have conveyed the sacrifice with our hymn.

Jamison Brereton Notes

viс╣гudr├║heva (that is, -─Б+iva) is quite problematic. Geldner refuses to tr., as does Scarlatta (245-46), though by classing it with -druh-compounds, he indicates a root affiliation. Acdg. to Renou, itтАЩs the equivalent of *druh├│ vi┼Ыuvс╣Ы╠Бt тАЬoppos├й au MalтАЭ or тАЬqui met le Mal en d├йrouteтАЭ; somewhat sim. K├╝mmel 484 тАЬWie die nach verschiedenen Seiten Tr├╝genden (?).тАЭ What all these suggestions have in common is the assumption that the 2nd member belong to тИЪdruh тАШdeceiveтАЩ. I suggest a different analysis, viс╣гud-r├║h-, where the 2nd member is the root noun to тИЪruh тАШmountтАЩ, and the first (viс╣гud-) is a deformed version of the already deformed adverb viс╣гvadry├аk тАШfacing in different directionsтАЩ, with the complex adverbial suffix found also in asmadry├аk тАШfacing towards usтАЩ. The empty -d- (/-t-) has been suffixed to the combining form viс╣гu- (/viс╣г┼л) underlying the adjective v├нс╣гva├▒c- тАШfacing in different directionsтАЩ. For the suggested phrase, cf. IX.75.1 r├бthaс╣Г v├нс╣гva├▒cam aruhat тАЬhe mounted the chariot that faces in different directonsтАЭ (with тИЪruh) and, with semantically related тИЪyuj and horses not chariot, VI.59.5 v├нс╣г┼лco ├б┼Ыv─Бn yuyuj─Бn├б ─лyate; X.79.7 v├нс╣г┼лco ├б┼Ыv─Бn yuyuje vanej─Б╠Бс╕е.

Griffith

Come to us ye who pour down wealth, come to the home which men must guard:
Like shafts, ye are made meet for sacrifice by song.

And this one, driving brightly, best of rivers at conveying,
the Sindhu River with her golden trackтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

I donтАЩt understand what the Sindhu is doing here. Is it a third place (besides the two in 17ab) where the A┼Ыvins might find exhilaration? Or is it a metaphor for the тАЬgood praiseтАЭ and/or тАЬbright insightтАЭ (both fem., as s├нndhu- is) in vs. 19? The agreements in vocabulary, ┼Ыveta- and the -y─Бvan/r-─л- cmpds, speak for the latter, but the former makes more sense to me.

тАЬA┼Ыvins, following a brilliant course, you acquire celebrity by the white river worthily praising you theenricher (of the peole on its banks).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

On its banks: the river is said to have praised the A┼Ыvins, as the с╣Ыс╣гi livedon its banks. These banks are golden, and consequently enrich those who live near

do you travel, o A┼Ыvins driving beautifully.

English translation:

тАЬYoke your chariot-drawing horses, V─Бyu; bring them, Vasu, encouraged (to the sacrifice); then drinkour Soma, come to our daily libations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Yoke the two that power the chariot; team up the two flourishing (horses), o good one.
After that, drink our honey, o V─Бyu; come to our pressings.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As often, h├н + IMPV marks the action of the h├н clause as the grounds for the subsequent clause (in this case c, as b is presumably parallel with a).

Griffith

Harness the steeds who draw the car, O Vasu, bring the well-fed pair.
O Vayu, drink thou of our meath: come unto our drink-offerings.

Auf, schirre dir die feisten an, o guter, die den Wagen ziehn, O Vaju, trinke unsern Meth und komm zu unsern Tr├дnken her.

English translation:

тАЬWe solicit your protection, V─Бyu, lord of sacrifice wonderful son-in- law of Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б: i.e.Brahm─Б; or, V─Бyu, the wind, having taken water from ─Аditya, fertilizes it, as rain, and is, therefore, as it were,his son-in-law, identifying Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б with ─Аditya (Yajus. 27.34)

Jamison Brereton

O V─Бyu, unerring lord of truth, son-in-law of Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАФyours are the forms of help we choose.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. с╣Ыtaspate, belonging to a hapax cmpd., has an unusual 1st member for a thematic stem. We should expect *с╣Ыtapate. But to construct that form is to confront its problem, a sequence of light syllables (4 in stem form). Rather than seeing anything archaic in the form we have, I think it likely that the cmpd was shaped in analogy to the numerous gen. -as-p├бti- with athem. gen., esp. bс╣Ы╠Бhas-p├бtiwith similar phonological shape. See also r├бthas-p├бti-, which shows the same anomaly as с╣Ыtaspate: comm. ad V.50.5. Unlike r├бthas-p├бti-, the form here makes no metrical problems.

Thy saving succour we elect.

English translation:

тАЬWe, the offerers of Soma, solicit riches from the sovereign, the son- in-law of Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б; (may webecome) wealthy.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The son-in-law of Tvaс╣гс╣нar, the lord of wealth, do we beseech for wealthтАФ
as the people who provide the pressed soma (we beseech) V─Бyu for
brilliant things.

Jamison Brereton Notes

r─Бy├б(с╕е) can be both gen. sg. and acc. pl., the former to be construed with ─л╠Б┼Ы─Бnam, the latter with ─лmahe, between which it is positioned. So already Oldenberg The identical p─Бdas (VI.54.8, VIII.46.6, 53.1) are susceptible to the same interpr.

Griffith

To Tvastar’s son-in-law we pray for wealth whereof he hath control:
For glory we seek vayu, men with juice effused.

Geldner

Des Tvastri Tochtermann, den M├дchtigen, bitten wir um Reicht├╝mer, um Herrlichkeit, den Vayu wir Leute bei gepre├Яtem Soma.

Grassmann

Des Tvaschtar Eidam flehn wir an, der ├╝ber vieles Gut verf├╝gt, Um Schatz den Vaju, trankversehne M├дnner wir.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬEstablish, V─Бyu, happiness in heaven; bear quickly your well-horsed (chariot); do you, who are mighty,yoke the broad-flanked (horses) to the car.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Happiness in heaven: V─Бyu is considered to be the supporter of allthe celestial luminaries, sarva jyotiс╣г─Бm tvad─Бdh─Бratv─Бt

Jamison Brereton

Kindly V─Бyu, journey here from heaven. Drive your good horse-flesh; drive from great (heaven) the two broad-winged (horses) at the chariot.

Griffith

From heaven, auspicious Vayu, come drive hither with thy noble steeds:
Come on thy mighty car with wide-extending seat.

English translation:

тАЬWe invoke you who are of graceful form, extending through your magnitude your limbs in all directions,to our religious rites, like the stone (for bruising the Soma).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

All directions: a┼Ыvapс╣Ыс╣гс╣нham = borne on a horse’sback;

A┼Ыva = vy─Бpta;

Pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нha = sarv─Бс╣Еga

Jamison Brereton

For we call you to the seats of men (to be) the first to attain delight (as we call) the horse-backed pressing stoneтАФ(call you) along with your munificence.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not think that V─Бyu is being compared directly to the pressing stone, but rather than we call on V─Бyu as we call on the pressing stone. Unfortunately this attenuates the force of the simile, but the various suggestions (Oldenberg, Geldner, Renou) as to why V─Бyu is like a horse-backed stone are so convoluted that I find them difficult to accept. The stone may be called horse-backed for two reasons: first, since the stones are also called s├│ma-pс╣Ыс╣гtha- (VIII.63.2) and soma is commonly identified as a horse, the identification has been transferred. It may also be that it also means тАШhaving the back of a horseтАЩ, that is, bowed or made for carrying.

Griffith

We call thee to the homes of men, thee wealthiest in noble food,
And liberal as a press-stone with a horse’s back.

Geldner

Grassmann

Zum M├дnnersitze laden wir dich ein, den sch├╢nstens schmausenden, Dem Steine gleich, der reichlich scharfen Soma tr├дgt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine V─Бyu, foremost (of the gods), exulting in your won mind, cause our rites to be productive of foodand water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Food and water: give us food and water, and so cause our rites to be duly performed

Jamison Brereton

O god V─Бyu, as the first to find exhilaration with your mind,
make prizes, waters, and insights for us.
The next group of hymns (27тАУ31) is attributed to Manu Vaivasvata and consists of four hymns to the All Gods, followed by a very interesting praise of the Sacrificer and his Wife, the only direct mention of this latter figure in the R╠еgveda. On the group see Oldenberg (1888: 215).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes ap├бс╕е for ├бpaс╕е тАШworkтАЩ, but this seems arbitrary. I tr. it as the acc. pl. тАШwatersтАЩ it appears to be.

Griffith

So, glad and joyful in thine heart, do thou, God, Vayu, first of all
Vouchsafe us water, strength, and thought.

Geldner

Indem du, Gott Vayu, in deinem Herzen dich als erster erg├╢tzest, schaff uns Belohnungen, ein Dichterwerk, gute Gedanken!

Grassmann

So schaffe du, o Vaju, her, erfreut im Herzen, bester du, O Gott, uns Speise, Trank, Verstand.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рджреЗрд╡+рд╡рд╛рдпреЛ) рд╣реЗ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдЧреБрдгрд╕рдореНрдкрдиреНрди рдирд╛рдпрдХ ! рдЬрд┐рд╕ рд╣реЗрддреБ рдЖрдк (рдордиреНрджрд╛рдирдГ) рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд┐рдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд┐рдд рдХрд░ рд░рд╣реЗ рд╣реИрдВ (рдЕрдЧреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ) рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЗ рдЕрдЧреНрд░рдЧрд╛рдореА рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЗрд╕рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдореН) рд╡рд╣ рдЖрдк (рдордирд╕рд╛) рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдорди рд╕реЗ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреН) рдЕрдиреНрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЕрдкрдГ) рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдЬрд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдзрд┐рдпрдГ) рдФрд░ рдЙрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣реЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдХреГрдзрд┐) рдмрдврд╝рд╛рд╡реЗрдВ реереирелрее

рд╢рд┐рд╡ рд╢рдВрдХрд░ рд╢рд░реНрдорд╛ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдиреА рдЕрдиреНрди, рдЬрд▓ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЛрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣ рдХреЛ рднреА рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдз рдЙрдкрд╛рдпреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдмрдврд╝рд╛рдпрд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ реереирелрее

рд╢рд┐рд╡ рд╢рдВрдХрд░ рд╢рд░реНрдорд╛ (рд╕рдВ) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрджреЗрд╡ рджрд░реНрд╢рдпрддрд┐ред

рд╢рд┐рд╡ рд╢рдВрдХрд░ рд╢рд░реНрдорд╛ (рд╕рдВ) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╡ ! рд╡рд╛рдпреЛ ! рдордирд╕рд╛=рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпреЗрди рдЪреЗрддрд╕рд╛ред рдордиреНрджрд╛рдирдГ=рд╣реГрд╖реНрдпрдиреНред рдЕрдЧреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ=рдЕрдЧреНрд░рдЧрд╛рдореАред рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдореНред рдирдГ=рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореНред рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреН=рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ред рдЕрдкрдГ=рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ред рдзрд┐рдпрдГ=рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ред рдХреГрдзрд┐=рдХреГрдгреБ реереирелрее
